The edge of the MW disc is visible in the increased multiplet counts at low |b|.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig5.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/94828296/stx1650fig5.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig5.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"94828296\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/471/2/10.1093_mnras_stx1650/1/stx1650fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611466529&Signature=eFczXpGaTRAKStIJbL8xflWEXzFUXsc1KBMKneU8sUZrfdFQduC1zYR63nvEkP27PNl8e1IvHv4zNPgM3FqYuu9PnLgaq10-NqsTPJJAzdPmq1RY0uzQfOTXJM2WSXjDyxAtkvSrmivX43nDgIvf4H4Sraw732SLgTOPZdL0pFOqjAFStWw7t1GnQb0Xge88DjFPvlivE9k3i3kGxpckFHFdHxk4xGVecbVYz9II74N6fxlYoZqX-JkSyhwz-qH3FABSgJWPRm1vn6ettYcYhld3l3qY2SqxU66Af9~GwjP344hhEr52Tv9uagUtGcRyIrv3MCugulbL7Ar9vt6oGw__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=94828296&ar=3922852&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig5.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Distribution of (non-duplicate) <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> singlets and multiplets over the pseudo-DES footprint. <em>Top:</em> density of single matches; <em>bottom:</em> ratio of multiplets to singlets, showing the same inhomogeneities identified from Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>. The edge of the MW disc is visible in the increased multiplet counts at low |<em>b</em>|.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/471/2/10.1093_mnras_stx1650/1/m_stx1650fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611466529&amp;Signature=Vfa1WI3rSfGeqnuvilBeknyssrHTDSYmyv5yA~Gs6v2D85e~Oj5qgqU1q3FF2OGWkHNbyH0~BVxXi~CfTrhgiMh6UBYmMaSW3nm4j5wl0dXWK6tx8MwjtPiihFIFuglEP5xHF9W~47jzx3m~faMhYypT4HQzKdKSusC03d-P7BvexDtPHswhyKe8fOtJo9QMECqbvVIqw8NELZjPDYpABFukh86nLDYEigauBGHclvXm5k4e-0pa1e7NL-2H~M0FmbDF4sAAEL5iXn197DbaBdfx9~vRFKVpPoa5-1NdlNe1xQgnhyu2vA5suY7Z9pcLXh4wCHlQSdPjizGVnq3Hhg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Distribution of (non-duplicate) WISE\u2212Gaia singlets and multiplets over the pseudo-DES footprint. Top: density of single matches; bottom: ratio of multiplets to singlets, showing the same inhomogeneities identified from Fig.\u00a02. The edge of the MW disc is visible in the increased multiplet counts at low |b|.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig5.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/94828296/stx1650fig5.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig5.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"94828296\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/471/2/10.1093_mnras_stx1650/1/stx1650fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611466529&Signature=eFczXpGaTRAKStIJbL8xflWEXzFUXsc1KBMKneU8sUZrfdFQduC1zYR63nvEkP27PNl8e1IvHv4zNPgM3FqYuu9PnLgaq10-NqsTPJJAzdPmq1RY0uzQfOTXJM2WSXjDyxAtkvSrmivX43nDgIvf4H4Sraw732SLgTOPZdL0pFOqjAFStWw7t1GnQb0Xge88DjFPvlivE9k3i3kGxpckFHFdHxk4xGVecbVYz9II74N6fxlYoZqX-JkSyhwz-qH3FABSgJWPRm1vn6ettYcYhld3l3qY2SqxU66Af9~GwjP344hhEr52Tv9uagUtGcRyIrv3MCugulbL7Ar9vt6oGw__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=94828296&ar=3922852&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig5.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Distribution of (non-duplicate) <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> singlets and multiplets over the pseudo-DES footprint. <em>Top:</em> density of single matches; <em>bottom:</em> ratio of multiplets to singlets, showing the same inhomogeneities identified from Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>. The edge of the MW disc is visible in the increased multiplet counts at low |<em>b</em>|.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Given the primary scope of this paper, i.e. lensed quasar searches, the identification of WG1, \u2026, WG4 may be regarded as an unintended by-product. Searches for Galactic substructure via stellar overdensities have been applied extensively in the past to the SDSS (Belokurov et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Zucker et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib69\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib69\" data-open=\"bib69\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Belokurov et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>; Irwin et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>; Koposov et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib33\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib33\" data-open=\"bib33\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>; Belokurov et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>), ATLAS (Belokurov et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>) and DES (Bechtol et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Koposov et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib34\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib34\" data-open=\"bib34\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Balbinot et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>; Li et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib38\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib38\" data-open=\"bib38\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>) footprints, and have also led to the discovery of two star clusters using <em>Gaia</em> data alone (Koposov et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). Northern streams, dwarf galaxies and globular clusters have also been found as overdensities in the PS1 footprint (e.g. Laevens et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Bernard et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>, and references therein). The search outlined here differs from those as it targets neighbours within the same 6\u201310\u00a0arcsec radius, as opposed to overdensities on arc-minute scales from binned star counts.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Two steps forward may be envisioned, enabling an all-sky <em>WISE</em>+<em>Gaia</em> search of Galactic substructure down to the <em>G</em>\u00a0=\u00a020.7 detection limit. First, it may be tailored directly on stellar objects (<em>W</em>1\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>2 \u2272 0.3, instead of <em>W</em>1\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>2\u00a0&gt;\u00a00.55), and may also be augmented with 2MASS (Skrutskie et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib57\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib57\" data-open=\"bib57\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>) information, such as <em>J</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>1\u00a0&lt;\u00a01.2 (Vickers, R\u00f6ser &amp; Grebel\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib63\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib63\" data-open=\"bib63\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). The quasar-like colour selection and match to <em>Gaia</em> are, in fact, one reason for the circular gaps in the distribution of multiplets over the sky, due to crowding or higher extinction. Second, while WG1, \u2026, WG4 were identified solely based on visual inspection, a more complete search may automatically select associations of multiplets that lie on the same line over \u22485\u201310\u00a0deg-long distances. This would also help identify more diffuse streams from more massive projenitors, which (Balbinot &amp; Gieles\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) can otherwise be confused with random fluctuations in the distribution of halo stars.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Even fainter magnitudes may be reached by trading the resolution of <em>Gaia</em> with deeper <em>grizY</em> magnitudes from DES in the South or PS1 in the North. In this case, the <em>WISE</em> pre-selection might be dropped altogether, by-passing completeness limits at <em>i</em> \u2273 21; however, a quasar-like <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia singlet</em> selection is still useful to characterize the survey coverage, and hence evaluate spurious substructure detections.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=94828300 id=\"94828300\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 CONCLUSIONS AND FUTURE PROSPECTS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">I have introduced two new methods to find quasar lenses, and illustrated their performance on publicly accessible footprints, using training- and test sets of known lenses and pairs in the CASTLES and SQLS data bases. The first concentrates on objects that are not well described as isolated quasars or blue galaxies; the second joins <em>WISE</em> and <em>Gaia</em> to detect multiplets of point-sources with overall quasar mid-IR colours. Besides recovering known lenses (with varying degree of success), both searches have led to new discoveries, reported elsewhere. A by-product of the <em>WISE</em>+<em>Gaia</em> search has been the identification of Galactic stream candidates that (as I later learned) are being found within the DES collaboration using different techniques.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">A common feature of many searches, including the outlier-selection and multiplet-detection, is the trade-off between completeness and manageable size of candidate samples to be visually inspected and followed-up at the telescope. Searches concentrating on \u2018lens\u2019 colours (e.g. this outlier-selection and the population-mixture classification by Williams et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib65\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib65\" data-open=\"bib65\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017a</a>) discard a high fraction of lenses with colours akin to nearby unlensed quasars. This is a price to pay in order to find systems with sources at higher redshift, or that could not be pre-selected for SDSS fibre spectroscopy due to their unusual colours. On the other hand, searches tailored on \u2018quasar\u2019 colours, amending the loss of lenses with quasar-like colours, result in large candidate samples to be examined: according to Ostrovski et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib47\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib47\" data-open=\"bib47\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), a double was found after eyeballing 5000 objects brighter than <em>i</em>\u00a0=\u00a019 in a 1500\u00a0deg<sup>2</sup> footprint. By comparison, the outlier selection resulted in 5064 SDSS targets brighter than <em>i</em>\u00a0=\u00a020.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The pseudo-distance cuts reduce the number of objects considerably, from 5\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>5</sup> to \u22488600 targets, of which \u224860\u2009per\u2009cent non-repeated objects, down to 239 final candidates, to the price of a harsh selection on known lenses. Even though few systems are rejected by each pair-wise combination of pseudo-distances, and most of the rejected lenses lie close to the cut boundaries, all cuts combined reduce the overall completeness to 30\u2009per\u2009cent, or 50\u2009per\u2009cent when only cuts in <em>d</em><sub>1</sub>, \u2026, <em>d</em><sub>4</sub> are used. Since the number of targets for visual inspection is manageable, one could loosen the cuts in <em>d</em><sub>5</sub>, \u2026, <em>d</em><sub>10</sub>; this would mean that the whole test set would now be a training-set for the method. Despite the 50\u2009per\u2009cent completeness with respect to already-known lenses, previously unknown lenses have been discovered with this technique (e.g. the new quad J1433+60; Agnello et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017b</a>), which suggests that outlier-selection is indeed complementary to previous searches.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Comparable numbers, from query to final candidates, are found when applying the <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> search to the SDSS footprint. The resolving power of <em>Gaia</em> enables multiplet detection for objects that are otherwise blended by the pipelines of ground-based surveys. New lenses, not found by other techniques, have been discovered with this method and will be presented elsewhere. Its performance, however, is not obvious to characterize: while it recognizes the two quasar images of the close double DES J0115 (Agnello et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015b</a>), and all quasar images of the fold PG1115 (Weymann et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib64\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib64\" data-open=\"bib64\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1980</a>), it detects only two images in the DES J0408 quad (Lin et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib39\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib39\" data-open=\"bib39\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), and two the WFI2033 quad (Morgan et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>), whereas the WFI2026 quad is seemingly unresolved. Due to <em>G</em>\u00a0=\u00a020.7 depth and pipeline-specific choices in resolving close pairs with high flux-ratios, roughly one every three known lenses/pairs is resolved by <em>Gaia</em>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Hybrid colours may be used as additional information, either using (limited) ground-based information or via <em>G</em><sub>RP</sub>, <em>G</em><sub>BP</sub> photometry, if available in future releases. This will be particularly interesting in view of the EUCLID mission, which should provide a wide-field, deep and sharp counterpart to the slitless spectroscopic Hamburg-ESO survey (Wisotzki et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib66\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib66\" data-open=\"bib66\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>), from which some remarkable quasar lenses have been identified.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Classification via clustering and outlier-selection has been implemented with different methods, for other purposes, over the last 2\u00a0yr. Clustering in colour-space has been used to evaluate photometric redshifts (Rahman et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib49\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib49\" data-open=\"bib49\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016b</a>; Rahman, M\u00e9nard &amp; Scranton\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib48\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib48\" data-open=\"bib48\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016a</a>), select LRGs (Rozo et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib51\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib51\" data-open=\"bib51\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>) and identify galaxy clusters from improved red-sequence finders (Rykoff et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib52\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib52\" data-open=\"bib52\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). Outlier-selection, implemented via random-forest classification on SDSS fibre spectra of galaxies, has been used to select peculiar galaxies of various types (Baron &amp; Poznanski\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). While the search in this paper was tailored on (lensed) quasars, and others were concentrated on galaxies, there is significant scope for integrating these into a comprehensive photometric classification across wide-field surveys and selection of the most peculiar objects.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">A by-product of the <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> multiplet search is the detection of (candidate) Milky Way streams, as coherent structures traced by stars in front of <em>WISE</em> quasar candidates. Multi-band follow-up is needed, however, to confirm them and characterize their stellar populations. A <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> search can be tailored on streams, using a different <em>WISE</em> selection and possibly augmenting with near-IR colours to separate extragalactic objects.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=94828308 id=\"94828308\" class=\"backacknowledgements-title\" >Acknowledgments</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">I wish to thank Eduardo Balbinot, Nora Shipp, Alex Drlica-Wagner for the comparison between my MW stream candidates and theirs; and Elizabeth Buckley-Geer, Huan Lin, Paul Schechter and Tommaso Treu for discussions on quasar lens searches. class=\"citation-links\"></div><div class=\"citation-links\"><div class=\"crossref-doi js-ref-link\"><a class=\"openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"http://dx.doi.org/10.1088/0004-637X/731/1/71\" target=\"_blank\">Search ADS</a></div><div class=\"xslopenurl empty-target\"><span class=\"inst-open-url-holders\" data-targetId=\"10.1088%2F0004-637X%2F731%2F1%2F71\">   <li class=\"toolbar-item item-pdf\">\r\n        <a class=\"al-link pdf article-pdfLink\" data-article-id=\"3922852\" href=\"/mnras/article-pdf/471/2/2013/19484061/stx1650.pdf\">\r\n            <img <div class=\"widget widget-ArticleFulltext widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=94828243 id=\"94828243\" class=\"abstract-title\" >Abstract</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">I describe two novel techniques originally devised to select strongly lensed quasar candidates in wide-field surveys. The first relies on outlier selection in optical and mid-infrared magnitude space; the second combines mid-infrared colour selection with <em>Gaia</em> spatial resolution, to identify multiplets of objects with quasar-like colours. Both methods have already been applied successfully to the Sloan Digital Sky Survey, ATLAS and Dark Energy Survey footprints: besides recovering known lenses from previous searches, they have led to new discoveries, including quadruply lensed quasars, which are rare within the rare-object class of quasar lenses. As a serendipitous by-product, at least four candidate Galactic streams in the South have been identified among foreground contaminants. There is considerable scope for tailoring the <em>WISE\u2212Gaia</em> multiplet search to stellar-like objects, instead of quasar-like, and to automatically detect Galactic streams.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;methods: statistical&quot;\">methods: statistical</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"surveys\">surveys</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;Galaxy: structure&quot;\">Galaxy: structure</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=94828245 id=\"94828245\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The many virtues of strongly lensed quasars, both for astrophysics and cosmography, are hampered by the relative paucity of systems with sufficient ancillary data. On the one hand, lensed quasars are valuable probes of cosmological distances and stellar and dark matter in <em>z</em> \u2248 1 galaxies (Courbin, Saha &amp; Schechter\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>): the delays between light curves of different quasar images can be translated in one-step measurements of the Hubble constant (Refsdal\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib50\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib50\" data-open=\"bib50\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1964</a>), making a low-redshift complement to cosmic microwave background experiments (Suyu et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib60\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib60\" data-open=\"bib60\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>); lens modelling and source-reconstruction enables super-resolved studies of quasar host galaxies at <em>z</em> \u2248 2 (Ding et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>); and micro-lensing yields a detailed view of the source central engine (Bate et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Sluse et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib59\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib59\" data-open=\"bib59\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Hutsem\u00e9kers et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) and luminous and dark mass in the deflector (Oguri, Rusu &amp; Falco\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib46\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib46\" data-open=\"bib46\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Schechter et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib54\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib54\" data-open=\"bib54\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). On the other hand, a few tens of these systems are currently known and few of them are suitable for time-delay cosmography or detailed lens modelling, whence the need for larger samples. With one every <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\mathcal {O}(10^4)$|</span> quasars being strongly lensed (Oguri &amp; Marshall\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib44\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib44\" data-open=\"bib44\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>), and \u22480.2 quasar lenses per square degree, these are a class of rare objects to be mined in wide-field surveys. In particular, predicted quasar lens samples are predominantly doubles, with only \u224814\u2009per\u2009cent being highly valuable quads.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Different searches, tailored to different data sets and surveys, have been developed to find new lensed quasars. The Cosmic Lens All Sky Survey (CLASS; Myers et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib43\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib43\" data-open=\"bib43\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>) and a parallel JVLA search (King et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib32\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib32\" data-open=\"bib32\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1999</a>) targeted radio-loud objects that could be resolved in multiple components by follow-up observations; the Sloan Quasar Lens Search (SQLS; Oguri et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib45\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib45\" data-open=\"bib45\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>) and its BOSS extension (BQLS; More et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib41\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib41\" data-open=\"bib41\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>) targeted objects that were identified as quasars from previous fibre spectroscopy. Both CLASS and SQLS/BQLS uncovered the bright end of the lensed quasar population, and were focused on either radio or UV excess pre-selection (for the challenges in observing radio-quiet lensed quasars; see e.g. Jackson et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). In order to expand this effort to fainter systems and higher redshift, a variety of techniques (Morgan et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>; Agnello et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015a</a>; Ostrovski et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib47\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib47\" data-open=\"bib47\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>; Williams, Agnello &amp; Treu\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib65\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib65\" data-open=\"bib65\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017a</a>) has been tailored to wide-field photometric and morphological searches.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Here, I illustrate two novel search methods that I have developed and used to discover new quasar lenses and whose performance has been complementary to other searches applied over the last year. The first, described in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a>, relies on outlier selection in the optical and mid-infrared, selecting lensed quasar targets among objects that do not \u2018obviously\u2019 belong to classes/clusters of more common contaminants. The second, described in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a>, combines the good spatial resolution and depth of the <em>Gaia</em> mission (Gaia Collaboration\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>; Lindegren et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>; van Leeuwen et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib62\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib62\" data-open=\"bib62\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) with a mid-infrared colour selection of quasar-like objects. Four new Galactic streams, found as a by-product of this method, are also briefly described. Given the setup of this search (tailored on quasar lenses), this discovery may be considered serendipitous, so I will outline how a similar search can be tailored on Galactic substructure. Concluding remarks are summarized in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>. Discoveries of quasar lenses from both methods, involving different collaborations, are reported elsewhere.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In what follows, some nomenclature will be consistently used. <em>Objects</em> are selected at query level from wide-field surveys, <em>targets</em> are a sub-sample of objects selected based on their catalogue properties, and <em>candidates</em> are a sub-sample of targets further selected based on their images either via visual inspection or cutout modelling. For the sake of brevity, I designate as quasar \u2018pairs\u2019 both physically associated quasars and chance alignments of quasars at different redshifts. The same holds for line-of-sight (LOS) quasar-star \u2018pairs\u2019.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Wide-field surveys are abbreviated as follows: SDSS is the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (Abazajian et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>); ATLAS is the VLT Survey Telescope ATLAS survey (Shanks et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib56\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib56\" data-open=\"bib56\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>); <em>WISE</em> is the Wide Infrared Survey Imager (Wright et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib68\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib68\" data-open=\"bib68\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>); DES is the Dark Energy Survey (S\u00e1nchez &amp; DES Collaboration\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib53\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib53\" data-open=\"bib53\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>); iPTF is the intermediate Palomar Transient Factory (Law et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib37\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib37\" data-open=\"bib37\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>) DR3 and PS1 is the first Pan-STARRS (Kaiser et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib31\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib31\" data-open=\"bib31\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Chambers et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>) telescope data release. Throughout this paper, <em>griz</em> magnitudes are in the AB system, and mid-infrared <em>W</em>1, <em>W</em>2, <em>W</em>3 magnitudes from <em>WISE</em> are in the Vega system.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=94828251 id=\"94828251\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 OUTLIER SELECTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Depending on the survey image quality and depth, and lens configuration and image separation, lensed quasars have colours intermediate between those of the source quasars and those of the deflector galaxies. Likewise, they can result in groups of point-like or extended sources, or as extended objects due to blending by image processing pipelines. Due to their rarity and intermediate colours and morphologies, lensed quasar candidate samples suffer from significant contamination by more common classes of objects. This problem can be mitigated by selecting objects that do <em>not</em> have typical colours of more common contaminants.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">As a <em>training</em> set for the outlier-selection method, I use the 10 quasar lenses and 40 false-positives in the morphologically selected sample of Inada et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>). This is because most quasar lenses are marginally deblended by the pipelines of ground-based surveys, and those with larger separation in previous searches have colours that are more typical of nearby quasars, due to the UVx and spectroscopic pre-selections that were applied there. The 10+40 morphological candidates of Inada et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) should then be a good guidance to a homogeneous sample of quasar-like objects with nearby companions, with different kinds of contaminants, and small enough that data mining techniques trained on it do not overspecialize, thus remaining complementary to previous searches.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">As a <em>test</em> set, to evaluate the method performance on a wider sample, I use a list of 149 known lenses compiled from the CASTLES<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn1\" data-open=\"fn1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">1</a></sup> data base and SQLS full sample from SDSS-DR7 given by Inada et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>). In particular, I will consider the 132 known systems with Dec.\u00a0&gt;\u00a0\u221220 for tests on the SDSS footprint. These are the same used by Williams et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib65\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib65\" data-open=\"bib65\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017a</a>) to evaluate the performance of population-mixture methods on quasar lenses in different ranges of image separation. Some of the outlier-selected targets were later found to be already known quasar lenses and pairs in the BQLS sample of More et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib41\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib41\" data-open=\"bib41\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>).</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=94828255 id=\"94828255\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-1>2.1 Setup, clusters and object classes</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In order to describe different populations in colour\u2013magnitude space, and similarly to previous work (Williams et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib65\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib65\" data-open=\"bib65\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017a</a>), I consider <em>g</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>r, g</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>i, r</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>z, i</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>1, <em>W</em>2, <em>W</em>1\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>2 and <em>W</em>2\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>3, compressing the catalogue information to a seven-dimensional <em>feature</em> space. I do not use UV excess information, since it is not always available in current wide-field surveys (e.g. DES), and it is less efficient at identifying quasars at redshifts <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> \u2273 2.5, where Ly\u2009\u03b1 emission exits the <em>u</em> band.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Object pre-selection is based on their extended morphology and some loose colour\u2013magnitude requirements. As a morphological pre-selection, I concentrate on objects that have<span class=\"monospace\">psf_r</span>-<span class=\"monospace\">mod_r</span>&gt;0.075 and <span class=\"monospace\">psf_i</span>-<span class=\"monospace\">mod_i</span>&gt;0.075 (referred below as <em>magnitude</em> criterion), or <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\log _{10}\\mathcal {L}_{star,i}&lt;-11$|</span> (resp. <em>stellarity</em> criterion).</p><div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">The <span class=\"monospace\">psf</span> and <span class=\"monospace\">model</span> magnitudes, as well as the <em>i</em>-band stellarity likelihood <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\log \\mathcal {L}_{star,i}=$|</span><span class=\"monospace\">lnLStar_i</span>, are taken directly from the SDSS catalogue.<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn2\" data-open=\"fn2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">2</a></sup> Their definition is, in fact, somewhat survey specific and different thresholds must be explored for ATLAS, DES and PS1, separately for each survey. Since this search is tailored on lensed quasars, I further select objects satisfying <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ1\" content-id=\"equ1\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray}\r\n&amp;&amp;{W1-W2&gt;0.55,\\ 2.2&lt;W2-W3&lt;3.8,}\\nonumber\\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{W1&lt;17.0, W2&lt;15.4, W3&lt;11.6,} \\nonumber\\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{\\delta W1&lt;0.25,\\ \\delta W2&lt;0.3,\\ \\delta W3&lt;0.35,} \\nonumber\\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{2.2&lt;i-W1&lt;5.75,\\ i-W3&lt;8.9,} \\nonumber\\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{g-i&lt;\\mathrm{max}(0.65; 1.2(i-W1)-2.4),} \\nonumber\\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{g-i&lt;2.55,\\ r-z&lt;1.5,\\ 15.0&lt;i&lt;20.5,}\r\n\\end{eqnarray} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(1)</span></div>which eliminates most stellar contaminants, blue galaxies and low-redshift quasars. Here, <em>griz</em> magnitudes are SDSS <span class=\"monospace\">model</span> magnitudes, <em>WISE W</em>\u2018X\u2019 magnitudes are <span class=\"monospace\">wXmpro</span> and \u03b4<em>W</em>\u2018X\u2019 are the uncertainties <span class=\"monospace\">wXsigmpro</span> on the corresponding magnitude (X = 1,2,3). Magnitude-selected extended objects will also be split into \u2018<span class=\"monospace\">c0</span>\u2019 objects, having <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ2\" content-id=\"equ2\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\nW2-W3&lt;\\mathrm{max}[2.7;\\, 3.15+1.5(W1-W2-1.075)],\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(2)</span></div>and \u2018<span class=\"monospace\">c1</span>\u2019 objects, occupying the remaining wedge in <em>WISE</em> colours. This colour distinction delimits the locus where all SQLS training-set objects lie, and roughly traces the distinction between quasar-dominated and galaxy-dominated objects (e.g. Wright et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib68\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib68\" data-open=\"bib68\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>).</div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Main contaminant classes are identified using Gaussian population mixture as a clustering algorithm, which has been validated as a means of object classification across different surveys (e.g. Bovy et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; DiPompeo et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Chehade et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>; Tie et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib61\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib61\" data-open=\"bib61\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>; Williams et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib65\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib65\" data-open=\"bib65\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017a</a>, where hybrid cuts on <em>g</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>i</em> and <em>i</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>1 similar to the above have been tested). A recurring theme of semisupervised clustering and classification methods is whether class parameters should be initialized: (i) based on where we expect different objects to lie a priori or (ii) identifying clusters independently and labelling them a posteriori. Here, I choose the second option, even though some clusters can be easily interpreted in terms of known object populations, as will be done below.</p><div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">Each class is then described by a mean <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\boldsymbol {\\mu }$|</span> and a covariance matrix <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\boldsymbol {\\Sigma }$|\u2060</span>. The relative class abundances will not be used at classification stage. To each object, with feature vector <strong>f</strong><sub><em>i</em></sub>, a pseudo-distance to the <em>k</em>th class is defined as <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ3\" content-id=\"equ3\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\nd_{i,k}=\\langle (\\mathbf {f}_{i}-\\boldsymbol {\\mu }_{k}),\\boldsymbol {\\Sigma }_{k}^{-1}(\\mathbf {f}_{i}-\\boldsymbol {\\mu }_{k})\\rangle /2.\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(3)</span></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The mean and covariance of each class are computed iteratively using Expectation\u2013Maximization. In order to ensure convergence, I borrow from the strategy of adaptive second moments (Bernstein &amp; Jarvis\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>): at each step in the computations of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\boldsymbol {\\mu }_{k}$|</span> and <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\boldsymbol {\\Sigma }_{k},$|</span> each object is additionally weighed with <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\mathrm{e}^{-d_{i,k}},$|</span> multiplying the covariances by 2. This avoids iteration instabilities due to neighbouring classes or \u2018large\u2019 widths in the classes. Some of the mean features are kept fixed, as they have values outside those of the queried sample (e.g. <em>W</em>1\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>2 of galaxies) or are unstable to Expectation\u2013Maximization.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The first four classes are common to objects selected via magnitude or stellarity morphological criteria. Most of the magnitude-selected sample is described by six clusters, whereas eight clusters are needed to encompass the majority of the stellarity-selected sample. Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> lists the averages <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\boldsymbol {\\mu }_{k}$|</span> and for the sake of brevity the widths <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\sqrt{\\Sigma _{k,jj}}$|</span> (<em>j</em>\u00a0=\u00a01, \u2026, 7) of the classes. By comparing the colours of different classes with those from spectroscopic subsamples (see e.g. Williams et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib65\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib65\" data-open=\"bib65\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017a</a>), one can roughly associate the first four classes with: (i) isolated quasars at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> \u2272 0.35, which have bright <em>W</em>2, high <em>i</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>1 and low <em>g</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>i</em> but can extend to redder colours due to contribution from their host galaxies; (ii) isolated quasars at redshift <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> \u2248 2, with fainter <em>W</em>2, <em>g</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>i</em> \u2272 0.6 and lower <em>i</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>1; (iii) narrow-line galaxies at <em>z</em> \u2248 0.2\u00a0\u2212\u00a00.3, with <em>W</em>2 and <em>i</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>1 comparable to <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> \u2248 2 quasars but higher <em>g</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>i</em> and (iv) fainter galaxies with <em>W</em>1\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>2 spanning a wide range. In fact, the empirical <em>WISE</em> colour\u2013magnitude cuts of Assef et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>) were designed to minimize contamination from the fourth class leaking into <em>WISE</em>-selected quasar samples.</p>                        <a id=\"94828263\" scrollto-destination=\"94828263\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl1\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table 1.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Means \u03bc<sub><em>k, j</em></sub> and widths <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\sqrt{\\Sigma _{k,ii}}$|</span> of the object clusters computed as in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2-1\"></span><a href=\"#sec2-1\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2.1</a>; the association between clusters and classes is done a posteriori, and described in the text.</p></div> </div><div class=\"table-overflow\"><table><thead><tr><th><em>k</em><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n .\u00a0</span></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1\u00a0</td><td>0.15\u00a0</td><td>0.44\u00a0</td><td>0.48\u00a0</td><td>4.34\u00a0</td><td>0.89\u00a0</td><td>\u2013\u00a0</td><td>2.80\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>\u00a0</td><td>0.31\u00a0</td><td>0.37\u00a0</td><td>0.21\u00a0</td><td>0.32\u00a0</td><td>0.14\u00a0</td><td>\u2013\u00a0</td><td>0.32\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>2\u00a0</td><td>0.32\u00a0</td><td>0.52\u00a0</td><td>0.25\u00a0</td><td>4.45\u00a0</td><td>0.55\u00a0</td><td>16.30\u00a0</td><td>3.90\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>\u00a0</td><td>0.20\u00a0</td><td>0.32\u00a0</td><td>0.29\u00a0</td><td>1.07\u00a0</td><td>0.61\u00a0</td><td>0.35\u00a0</td><td>0.50\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>3\u00a0</td><td>0.16\u00a0</td><td>0.14\u00a0</td><td>0.00\u00a0</td><td>3.60\u00a0</td><td>1.24\u00a0</td><td>14.90\u00a0</td><td>2.94\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>\u00a0</td><td>0.10\u00a0</td><td>0.13\u00a0</td><td>0.17\u00a0</td><td>0.15\u00a0</td><td>0.11\u00a0</td><td>0.47\u00a0</td><td>0.15\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>4\u00a0</td><td>0.95\u00a0</td><td>1.40\u00a0</td><td>0.78\u00a0</td><td>3.51\u00a0</td><td>0.55\u00a0</td><td>\u2013\u00a0</td><td>3.5\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>\u00a0</td><td>0.24\u00a0</td><td>0.30\u00a0</td><td>0.16\u00a0</td><td>0.41\u00a0</td><td>0.40\u00a0</td><td>\u2013\u00a0</td><td>0.55\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>5\u00a0</td><td>0.35\u00a0</td><td>0.61\u00a0</td><td>0.61\u00a0</td><td>4.17\u00a0</td><td>0.82\u00a0</td><td>14.19\u00a0</td><td>3.12\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>\u00a0</td><td>0.16\u00a0</td><td>0.18\u00a0</td><td>0.16\u00a0</td><td>0.48\u00a0</td><td>0.13\u00a0</td><td>0.32\u00a0</td><td>0.20\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>6\u00a0</td><td>0.48\u00a0</td><td>0.88\u00a0</td><td>0.84\u00a0</td><td>4.16\u00a0</td><td>0.92\u00a0</td><td>13.90\u00a0</td><td>2.35\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>\u00a0</td><td>0.25\u00a0</td><td>0.25\u00a0</td><td>0.12\u00a0</td><td>0.47\u00a0</td><td>0.21\u00a0</td><td>0.48\u00a0</td><td>0.36\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>7\u00a0</td><td>0.22\u00a0</td><td>0.25\u00a0</td><t class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/94828263\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=94828264 id=\"94828264\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-2>2.2 Adapting on SQLS training set</h3>\r\n<div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">Once the classes/clusters are defined, targets must be selected based on how far they lie from different classes. In order to do so, I use linear combinations of the pseudo-distances <em>d<sub>k</sub></em>. The first set of pseudo-distance cuts, using <em>d</em><sub>1</sub>, \u2026, <em>d</em><sub>4</sub> as <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ4\" content-id=\"equ4\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray}\r\n&amp;&amp;{d_1\\ge 4.5, d2\\ge 15, d_4\\ge 4,} \\nonumber\\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{12d_2-17\\ge d_3\\ge 225-3d_2,} \\nonumber\\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{d_3\\ge 175-10d_1, d_3\\ge 6d_1-20,} \\nonumber\\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{125-4d_4&lt; d_3\\le 100d_4}\r\n\\end{eqnarray} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(4)</span></div>is displayed in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>. Some of the cuts can be made more or less restrictive, with the aim of retaining as many quasar-like systems as possible, while rejecting galaxies and SQLS false-positives without penalizing the SQLS true-positives.</div>                        <a id=\"94828266\" scrollto-destination=\"94828266\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/471/2/10.1093_mnras_stx1650/1/m_stx1650fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611466529&amp;Signature=VaUMj9rh4T1NknzdWLjnm7T91HGsrxDD5VVzucOpdBP446tOlt4vqU7MSydHAC6QmGKCatc4LQ9fTug2dK23hGarjklgskQfwaZrfbMWoe7opGLwCRVFVOln09jQZfk2X6nr8uZ7~QiIJnBjJOnwjghsWFZh7BXGmr42zO56Jb2fYctVVT9z-NrryjiC-q2CCbWzWTaOldRkyur-c6avFpy-azpZRzh6Ugpnq1KADqi9OTO5ZhYp0hmNv7LdtDDJirmL8wt38e-ExczWXQ5Bfqt33gcgJvImu2EqxNvDSpcoCo6aj~7qjWW8g1Gti1ge1Qg9N~DcqRb86HFs9IndTA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Cuts in pseudo-distances from main clusters/classes. The axes are shown mostly as a guidance to the eye.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig1.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/94828266/stx1650fig1.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig1.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"94828266\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/471/2/10.1093_mnras_stx1650/1/stx1650fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611466529&Signature=ALIkiQTGLkizlNtUQVz0zolnK9bFn4iqDyKIcdhBX3-Ik4kk04-OM4WwYN8mRqY4reHlrfQ8tRj4VOAZX5yvZ9dHUCxbe~wQVBuHInb-5lIqF73SoSIZOmtaJOAe2qDc9weTw5s5rrXbNBUON5~reRj0-S8Mh3rh4np22m9nAWnM4bscC~5ep0T2rDgIwN~Gu6eCrszQ~UDMBOGzinctdeojuXhcyJI5gkGTVFg8j5VM8REUmrhLgMDXD6wSort5UbMZq8EsakoBT~KKRVfTC8eaosHxVwlTtJyNBLmnAlKb00z~txgmjhiGWccgD-9L5ZIlSNrTrd4eyMUOjlBwaA__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=94828266&ar=3922852&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig1.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Cuts in pseudo-distances from main clusters/classes. Red (resp.) black bullets mark SQLS lenses (resp. false positives) in the training set. <em>Top:</em> First set of cuts on <em>d</em><sub>1</sub>, \u2026, <em>d</em><sub>4</sub>; grey (resp. purple) swarms trace magnitude-selected (resp. stellarity-selected) objects. <em>Bottom:</em> Cuts in <em>d</em><sub>5</sub>, \u2026, <em>d</em><sub>10</sub> depending on the extended-morphology criterion; light-blue bullets mark the candidates selected after visual inspection of the first-pass targets, and <span class=\"monospace\">c0</span> (resp. <span class=\"monospace\">c1</span>) targets correspond to high <em>d</em><sub>6</sub> (resp. <em>d</em><sub>5</sub>). The axes are shown mostly as a guidance to the eye.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">With this combination, 9 out of 10 training-set lenses are retained, and 20 out of 40 false-positives are rejected. At face value, this would mean that outlier selection is 90\u2009per\u2009cent complete with respect to the SQLS and has half as many contaminants, but matters are more complicated. One the one hand, the SQLS and BQLS relied on spectroscopic information, so contamination by narrow-line galaxies is completely suppressed there, while it is non-negligible in photometric searches. On the other, the same spectroscopic pre-selection limits the SQLS and BQLS to objects for which spectra are available, and has in fact precluded the discovery of some noteworthy lenses.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">When the first cuts of equations (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-equ1\"></span><a href=\"#equ1\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">1</a>) and (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-equ4\"></span><a href=\"#equ4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>) are applied to objects in the SDSS-DR12 footprint, 8543 (resp. 15839) objects are still left in the magnitude-selected (resp. stellarity-selected) sample.<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn3\" data-open=\"fn3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">3</a></sup> In the colour\u2013colour diagrams of remaining objects, there are some overdensities corresponding to (apparently) isolated quasars with <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.5\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1, based on the available fibre spectra. Their <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\boldsymbol {\\mu }$|</span> values are different between magnitude-selected (two clusters, <em>k</em>\u00a0=\u00a05, 6) and stellarity-selected (four clusters, <em>k</em>\u00a0=\u00a07, \u2026, 10) objects. The lower panels of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> show where objects surviving the cuts of equation (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-equ4\"></span><a href=\"#equ4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>) lie in terms of the distances from additional clusters (<em>d</em><sub>5</sub>, \u2026, <em>d</em><sub>10</sub>).</p><div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">To further guide the selection, I visually inspected the first-pass targets and retained 82 magnitude-selected and 157 stellarity-selected candidates, which are not \u2018obvious\u2019 kinds of contaminants such as blue galaxies or nearby quasars and Seyfert galaxies. Their pseudo-distance distribution, occupying mostly the outskirts of the object clusters (see Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>), suggests the following cuts <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ5\" content-id=\"equ5\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n0.15d_6 -1.5\\le d_5\\le 1.75d_6+10\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(5)</span></div>for magnitude-selected objects, and <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ6\" content-id=\"equ6\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray}\r\n&amp;&amp;{2.0d_7+7\\ge d_8\\ge 0.25d_7 -3,} \\nonumber\\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{d_{10}\\le 4.5d_8+10,\\ d_9\\le 10d_8+10 }\r\n\\end{eqnarray} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(6)</span></div>for stellarity-selected objects. Once applied to the first-pass candidates, they result in 3728 magnitude-selected and 4712 stellarity-selected targets, 60\u2009per\u2009cent of which are non-repeated catalogue entries. This has reduced the initial \u22485\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>5</sup> queried objects to a manageable sample for visual inspection; in fact, the cuts in <em>d</em><sub>1</sub>, \u2026, <em>d</em><sub>4</sub> were already enough to obtain a reasonable reduction in objects to be inspected, whence the 82 + 157 candidates were obtained.</div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=94828270 id=\"94828270\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-3>2.3 Blind test on SDSS</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Using the CASTLES+SQLS <em>test</em> set introduced above, we can quantify how many known lenses are lost at each stage and why. At pre-selection level, 57 of the 132 test objects are retained, due primarily to the extendedness criteria as noticed already by Williams et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib65\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib65\" data-open=\"bib65\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017a</a>), and secondarily to <em>WISE</em> colour selection. Of these, 35 remain after the first cuts (in equation\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-equ4\"></span><a href=\"#equ4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>); 36 satisfy equations (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-equ5\"></span><a href=\"#equ5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>) and (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-equ6\"></span><a href=\"#equ6\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">6</a>) and only 22 satisfy the cuts in all pseudo-distances. Most of the rejected lenses lie close to the selection boundaries, which could be re-adjusted post hoc to increase the completeness. However, I preferred to perform a blind test of this method, trained solely on 10 lenses and 40 non-lenses.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> shows the distribution of queried objects (grey swarm), candidates selected after <em>d</em><sub>1</sub>, \u2026, <em>d</em><sub>4</sub> cuts (blue bullets) and known lenses (red star symbols). One every 40 queried objects is shown, for convenience. Inhomogeneous spatial coverage is a direct consequence of the SDSS scanning, and affects the distribution of targets, candidates and known lenses. Candidates and known lenses have compatible distributions in <em>WISE</em> colours (not used by previous campaigns) and morphological parameters.</p>                        <a id=\"94828273\" scrollto-destination=\"94828273\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig2\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 2.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/471/2/10.1093_mnras_stx1650/1/m_stx1650fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611466529&amp;Signature=yY8vPuT-iAkWIz7euc9tC7lhSeVfO6ykQJMy~36tEHEXitMxbwJHdWehLu1GKd9~CSXSO2pSYUuY3UL~g6-lhcpnrrrqXazJ~KgodCBUzIsrNpVmrmVcSKAClTNsN3mt6K0evws30Tdpirgzx~xDYi3iZ88Fdj0CA1oYGaM49SbIOEwgqlvI6MkxbBiTiIdhVYgb9V0iKKJn5tSKNrGv8-w82Cbj1hAL9rVXMsZC~OCe6THbB9w57355XbVK30s16iU7C9h4eFpnwp4dkgmq5xl2FNWEbBD4W1zM1fL95XFY2gyzdg0EV0VVGHRhLIf6K4lBcqjccLwFE0ojFwjBxw__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Distribution of query-selected objects (grey), candidates (light-blue bullets) and known lenses (red stars). The SDSS coverage is not homogeneous, as reflected at all stages of query, target- and candidate-selection and by the known systems, which have consistent distributions in WISE colours and stellarity/psf-mod distribution. The axes are shown mostly as a guidance to the eye.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig2.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/94828273/stx1650fig2.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig2.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"94828273\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/471/2/10.1093_mnras_stx1650/1/stx1650fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611466529&Signature=kDaGPGMlAanRyKfB9NPvxah772x4jUyWAILgFFfCPWPlgCLqRfjaVjTbk9RuI1vkPwUKhX2eVhCfOggH-1aU7ilEciJpTuP9BdZq2k-cckvG62Q~OTB4zJxmNcUSD3~ndflIlsfoDb9cyaU-qcsy99zI3iqnqwqI2-evlKQQ0S3to01Is9Ioex6fMJsEVqwjFX9WC86DP982H7c0ORZAokePj~EPYx0uCTuHQ1cY0BLbpuij3BlWxwpPo2gAQuMqR1RI4CIvZMdvY7Mf3j8Ru3jAiUoclohqo432R0G3syddGdJyIloc67-7mBe6C5kPrHICT5ij74goDXAzmRPNvQ__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=94828273&ar=3922852&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig2.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Distribution of query-selected objects (grey), candidates (light-blue bullets) and known lenses (red stars). The SDSS coverage is not homogeneous, as reflected at all stages of query, target- and candidate-selection and by the known systems, which have consistent distributions in WISE colours and stellarity/psf-mod distribution. The axes are shown mostly as a guidance to the eye.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig2.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/94828273/stx1650fig2.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig2.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"94828273\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/471/2/10.1093_mnras_stx1650/1/stx1650fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611466529&Signature=kDaGPGMlAanRyKfB9NPvxah772x4jUyWAILgFFfCPWPlgCLqRfjaVjTbk9RuI1vkPwUKhX2eVhCfOggH-1aU7ilEciJpTuP9BdZq2k-cckvG62Q~OTB4zJxmNcUSD3~ndflIlsfoDb9cyaU-qcsy99zI3iqnqwqI2-evlKQQ0S3to01Is9Ioex6fMJsEVqwjFX9WC86DP982H7c0ORZAokePj~EPYx0uCTuHQ1cY0BLbpuij3BlWxwpPo2gAQuMqR1RI4CIvZMdvY7Mf3j8Ru3jAiUoclohqo432R0G3syddGdJyIloc67-7mBe6C5kPrHICT5ij74goDXAzmRPNvQ__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=94828273&ar=3922852&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig2.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Distribution of query-selected objects (grey), candidates (light-blue bullets) and known lenses (red stars). The SDSS coverage is not homogeneous, as reflected at all stages of query, target- and candidate-selection and by the known systems, which have consistent distributions in <em>WISE</em> colours and stellarity/<span class=\"monospace\">psf-mod</span> distribution. The axes are shown mostly as a guidance to the eye.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">This outlier-selection seems to retain known quads and doubles alike. Some lenses are present multiple times in the queried sample, the most popular being: J2343\u22120050 (78 matches, m.), J1001+5553 (20\u00a0m.), J0145\u22120945 (7\u00a0m.), J1206+4332 (6\u00a0m.), J0806+2006 (5\u00a0m.), J1304+2001 (4\u00a0m.). Besides these, 10 lenses are flagged 3\u00a0times by the object query, and 20 are flagged twice. Some BQLS objects, not included in the test set, have been rediscovered as well. When applied to the DES catalogue, with suitably translated magnitudes (as discussed by Agnello et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017a</a>), it recognized both large-separation lenses like DES0408 (Lin et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib39\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib39\" data-open=\"bib39\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) and small-separation blends like DES0115 (Agnello et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015b</a>). The main reason is that, while all these lenses have markedly quasar-like <em>WISE</em> colours, their hybrid colours are not typical of unlensed and low-redshift quasars.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Whether quasar \u2018pairs\u2019, which are interesting for other applications, are eliminated or retained depends chiefly on how much their overall colours resemble those of low-redshift quasars. Based on the results of different spectroscopic follow-up campaigns,<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn4\" data-open=\"fn4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">4</a></sup> quasar pairs with sources at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> \u2248 2 are present among quasar lens candidates. Some quasar pairs with nearly identical spectra are also present, but whether they are lenses or physically associated quasars will require deeper follow-up.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=94828276 id=\"94828276\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 GAIA MULTIPLET DETECTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">By using different all-sky surveys, one can combine their separate advantages and exploit the largest possible footprint. In particular: <em>WISE</em> enables a mid-IR selection of quasar-like objects, gathering the light from different quasar images within the same \u22486\u00a0arcsec beam; while <em>Gaia</em> offers higher spatial resolution, enabling a distinction between isolated quasars and quasars with companions within the same <em>WISE</em> beam. From this viewpoint, combining <em>WISE</em> and <em>Gaia</em> for quasar lens searches is reminiscent of the CLASS/JVLA strategy of radio-loud detection and higher resolution follow-up.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Here, I illustrate the general properties of objects selected with <em>WISE W</em>1, <em>W</em>2, <em>W</em>3 and <em>Gaia</em> DR1 data, using the CASTLES+SQLS known systems as guidance. With the addition of SQLS quasar pairs, the test set amounts to 197 objects. Visual inspection is needed to obtain a candidate sample, so I will explore the performance of this combined search over three footprints: one covering the SDSS-DR12; one covering the ATLAS-DR3; and one covering slightly more than the DES-Y3. For SDSS and ATLAS, I will also rely on public survey catalogues and images, whereas for the DES footprint I will delineate some general properties based solely on <em>WISE</em> and <em>Gaia</em> data. To quantify how many lens candidates can be expected with this method, I select objects with <em>W</em>1, <em>W</em>2, <em>W</em>3 as in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a> (over the three considered footprints) and match them to <em>Gaia</em> using a 6\u00a0arcsec search radius. In the SDSS and ATLAS, when <em>griz</em> catalogue magnitudes are available, I also require that objects satisfy the colour\u2013magnitude requirements of equations (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-equ1\"></span><a href=\"#equ1\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">1</a>) and (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-equ2\"></span><a href=\"#equ2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a>). As a separate footprint, to examine the role of hybrid optical-IR colours, I will study objects with Dec. &gt;\u221230\u00a0deg that are detected also in the iPTF catalogue. These have the advantage that they can also be visually inspected using PS1 images, and that quasar-like objects can be further selected based on their variability signatures (Schmidt et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib55\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib55\" data-open=\"bib55\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">As an illustration of the method, and to minimize contamination by star-quasar pairs, the <em>WISE</em>\u2013<em>Gaia</em> matches will be performed on objects with <em>G</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a015.0 and |<em>b</em>|\u00a0&gt;\u00a020.0 and visually inspected for |<em>b</em>|\u00a0&gt;\u00a030.0 when possible. This is also why the recent quad candidate of Berghea et al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) is discarded at pre-selection, while (at least) four known quads are retained: HE0435 (Wisotzki et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib67\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib67\" data-open=\"bib67\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>), RXJ1131 (Sluse et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib58\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib58\" data-open=\"bib58\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>), PG1115 and SDSS J1433+60.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=94828280 id=\"94828280\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3-1>3.1 General behaviour</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Most known lenses and pairs correspond to one detection per system in <em>WISE</em>, whereas 55 of them are recognized as separate objects in <em>Gaia</em>-DR1. Their overall properties are summarized in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>: the <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> match can be performed down to <em>G</em>\u00a0=\u00a020.7; most lenses with a <em>Gaia</em> multiplet counterpart have <em>G</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a020; and the flux-ratios of different components are not extreme, mostly |2.5log<sub>10</sub>(<em>f</em><sub>1</sub>/<em>f</em><sub>2</sub>)|\u00a0\u2272\u00a02.</p>                        <a id=\"94828282\" scrollto-destination=\"94828282\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/471/2/10.1093_mnras_stx1650/1/m_stx1650fig3.jpeg?Expires=1611466529&amp;Signature=Ppn-FtDu3BSPnpJ-k4ZoHbF~cDH-RBNLYMDrWhkgpxlUn-Au8mGPgiQNa8o-qWI6rYZ4kpxglOMyZpuZNq1rk-4vQ4NDNYy5aRsI9315HKtqaW~F311IesY4lHSgW3nP19OCRlqJqMBz9Kn8HPQrpcOwGSpUa92qpNBgWs0hayDTk1u8MFQwEDsp1epxoIE5hxQnIqLTDD1GL~5sbXQcBppLvwcwR4il-4RJWYrv1ddPloakKTWTVaoEqNpu4fk7xGFzPkPHzA1fFM07qT223W4KUbY4M2yQLz~8lKei9imFjOp809Ea6fFM7YUf87OtufsxpWvg61Q~knWIF9PUtA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Top: Total magnitude versus magnitude difference of individually resolved components, for WISE objects split by Gaia. The lines delimit systems with a faintest image with <em>G</em>\u00a0=\u00a020 (full) or <em>G</em>\u00a0=\u00a021. (dashed). <em>Middle:</em> Spatial distribution of <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> multiplets Grey (resp. purple, black) points correspond to the SDSS (resp. ATLAS-DR3, pseudo-DES) footprint. In both panels, red bullets indicate known quasar lenses/pairs. <em>Bottom: WISE\u2212Gaia</em> multiplets with Dec. &gt;\u221230; the dashed contours correspond to <em>b</em>\u00a0=\u00a0\u00b130\u00a0deg.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The grey points in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a> display general properties of the <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> multiplets, for a random sub-set, showing the same behaviour as for the known lenses in red. This first match results in 1868 multiplets in SDSS-DR12, 648 in ATLAS-DR3, and 2679 in the approximate DES footprint. All of these are manageable numbers for a quick visual inspection, and have led to new lenses being discovered with this method, which will be reported elsewhere.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Exploiting the homogeneous (sometimes spectroscopic) coverage of SDSS, we can further quantify the fraction of promising multiplets. A quick visual inspection reveals different contaminant classes: galaxy groups and mergers; stars, especially at low galactic latitudes |<em>b</em>|\u00a0&lt;\u00a033\u00a0deg; quasar-star and quasar-galaxy LOS alignments. Those that are not \u2018obvious\u2019 contaminants amount to 127 candidates, some more convincing than others. By construction, they include known lenses with different configurations (quads and doubles) and image separations.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The situation in other footprints is complicated by the patchy (ATLAS) or limited (DES) coverage of public catalogues. Visual inspection of ATLAS-DR3 targets with at least one valid magnitude results in 28 unique candidates. The known quad RXJ1131 is flagged four times by this search (corresponding to its four quasar images), even though it is covered just in <em>i</em> band in the public footprint. Visual inspection produces one candidate every 20\u201330 targets, so one can expect 60\u2013100 candidates to be selected in the DES footprint with this method; the depth, image-quality and <em>grizY</em> coverage of DES also help to further select the most promising systems for follow-up.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Since the multiplet search targets objects with quasar-like <em>WISE</em> colours and nearby neighbours, it also retains LOS alignments of quasars and stars. This aspect is further discussed below.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=94828287 id=\"94828287\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3-2>3.2 Hybrid colours</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Since hybrid colours help separate quasar-like objects from galaxies and stars, an ideal search would incorporate the multiplet information from <em>Gaia</em> with optical/IR colours to reduce contamination. The top panel in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>, displaying hybrid colours with <em>Gaia</em>, SDSS and <em>WISE</em>, suggests that these may still be used to aid the <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> multiplet detection in the case of partial (e.g. only <em>i</em> band) ground-based coverage. There, I am using 0.175\u00a0+\u00a0<em>G</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>i</em> (green points) instead of <em>g</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>i</em> (grey swarm) to quantify the red excess of SDSS objects corresponding to <em>Gaia</em> multiplets. Indeed, most quasar-like objects have compatible colours across SDSS and <em>Gaia</em>. Some objects have <em>G</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>i</em> versus <em>i</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>1 falling beyond the pre-selection boundaries, and may be LOS pairs of quasars and stars that are resolved by <em>Gaia</em> but not by the SDSS.</p>                        <a id=\"94828289\" scrollto-destination=\"94828289\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig4\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 4.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/471/2/10.1093_mnras_stx1650/1/m_stx1650fig4.jpeg?Expires=1611466529&amp;Signature=xAB0uWOebOCF0oKNF20Pz4QIonKXgN9o8o30ZUmqQPT2IVThPeb3kQlslmZ4pFQLROA32xC-knNnVl6NeguleOvUo69-anT-VaFueHtqn8zs1J26nt9DJfyYn64hkDlgWm1bGyBQr-L9A09U~WvFIsy1-2h8GKtsOIXgkg~3UeXbqEZrUvCO1Yc8uMijQnwsWJpwt48N3tTYnQ0UFRZiTbTKkKxlwWKuCvBg7xil7maU6iaZynK1fz86XCVYarSqETlsagbx1rOT-7v9djY5ZD3hYtxK4~FY9Fl1zbCYXnfSLKZ0WsI5nkLUMsyXxzA-H7NgUvJ91ckpMLNVXINLlQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Using hybrid colours across three surveys, for patchy ground-based coverage. red bullets indicate known lenses.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig4\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 4.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/471/2/10.1093_mnras_stx1650/1/m_stx1650fig4.jpeg?Expires=1611466529&amp;Signature=xAB0uWOebOCF0oKNF20Pz4QIonKXgN9o8o30ZUmqQPT2IVThPeb3kQlslmZ4pFQLROA32xC-knNnVl6NeguleOvUo69-anT-VaFueHtqn8zs1J26nt9DJfyYn64hkDlgWm1bGyBQr-L9A09U~WvFIsy1-2h8GKtsOIXgkg~3UeXbqEZrUvCO1Yc8uMijQnwsWJpwt48N3tTYnQ0UFRZiTbTKkKxlwWKuCvBg7xil7maU6iaZynK1fz86XCVYarSqETlsagbx1rOT-7v9djY5ZD3hYtxK4~FY9Fl1zbCYXnfSLKZ0WsI5nkLUMsyXxzA-H7NgUvJ91ckpMLNVXINLlQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Using hybrid colours across three surveys, for patchy ground-based coverage.
