Gaia multiplet counterparts). Lower panels: Hybrid colours of WISE\u2212Gaia multiplets that also fall in the iPTF footprint, with purple (resp. blue) indicating objects with lower (resp. higher) R\u00a0\u2212\u00a0W1; red bullets indicate known lenses.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig4.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/94828289/stx1650fig4.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig4.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"94828289\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/471/2/10.1093_mnras_stx1650/1/stx1650fig4.jpeg?Expires=1611466529&Signature=t1-uj6Xv6WozBMYRY6mgdQ05GFdI6VSCKvwLLbRRo5bO-vE-caG59VHH-VRMauMAoAfGZU5wBh0KxrZJQ48YebrdWa4TSW7zDQhhDoKzPLJKCrLRvnfjFBfgMOAP3kJ6spltoQ7GQjDerEP5zoq3CpLlOVuYPbmJaSkhVUJY6KJB4z20XnejY6fXOMBcCrrNNVi3bztxf~Bd9u0w1JP9HHqAGVUWmOQNmrNQTZVaOTcozFCxFmSGXy2hjrfKCTmtjIkhq7Na2eJbjWe7HH2K7xzJ2dUNJDQrfZBnTnsSLZe8DU4HDt9rY-~jBXvSExZrO1tAAyHPOsb8meDRmMTZVg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=94828289&ar=3922852&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig4.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Using hybrid colours across three surveys, for patchy ground-based coverage. <em>Top:</em> Grey (resp. green) points show <em>g</em><sub>sdss</sub>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>i</em><sub>sdss</sub> (resp. 0.175\u00a0+\u00a0<em>G</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>i</em><sub>sdss</sub>) versus <em>i</em><sub>sdss</sub>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>1 for SDSS queried objects (resp. <em>Gaia</em> multiplet counterparts). <em>Lower</em> panels: Hybrid colours of <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> multiplets that also fall in the iPTF footprint, with purple (resp. blue) indicating objects with lower (resp. higher) <em>R</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>1; red bullets indicate known lenses.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">A similar scenario is shown by matching <em>WISE</em>\u2013<em>Gaia</em> objects (singlets and multiplets) with the iPTF. The lower panels in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a> shows their hybrid colours across the three surveys, with <em>R</em> band from the iPTF when available. Similarly to the pseudo-DES footprint, objects were selected based only on <em>WISE</em> colours, so a large contamination by LOS quasar-star pairs is present, as seen in the spatial distribution of multiplets: many abound at |<em>b</em>|\u00a0&lt;\u00a030\u00a0deg, besides clumps corresponding to M31 and M33. In terms of colours, flux ratios <em>G</em><sub>1</sub>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>G</em><sub>2</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.5log<sub>10</sub>(<em>f</em><sub>1</sub>/<em>f</em><sub>2</sub>) and separations, different object classes can be recognized: (i) quasar-like objects, with <em>R</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>1\u00a0\u2273 2.8, <em>R</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>2 \u2273 3.9, themselves divided in three main clusters at <em>W</em>1\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>2\u00a0=\u00a0(0.750\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.125), (0.94\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.07), (1.225\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.175); (ii) quasar-star pairs in which the star dominates in the optical, with low iPTF-<em>WISE</em> colours and <em>G</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>R</em> \u2248 \u22120.02\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.05, with object separations distributed smoothly and regardless of colours; (iii) \u2018bluer\u2019 objects, with <em>G</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>R</em> \u2272 \u22120.2, |<em>G</em><sub>1</sub>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>G</em><sub>2</sub>| \u2272 2.0, and typical separations \u22735.0\u00a0arcsec.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Different object classes are all intersecting, at least in projection, and again the known quasar lenses and pairs seem to occupy the outskirts of different populations. Quasar-star objects with low <em>R</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>1 seem just the visible \u2018tip of the contaminant iceberg\u2019, since multiplets with |<em>b</em>|\u00a0&lt;\u00a030\u00a0deg (perhaps mostly quasar-star pairs) form a tight sequence with <em>G</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>R</em> \u2248 \u22120.02\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.05 but extend to higher values of <em>R</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>1, depending on the relative contribution of quasar and star. Since quasars dominate in the infrared, the <em>WISE W</em>1\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>2, <em>W</em>2\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>3 colours or quasar-star pairs are indistinguishable from those of isolated and lensed quasars.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The analysis of hybrid colours suggests that an integrated approach, incorporating both the multiplet detection and outlier selection, may yield cleaner lens candidate samples. This has not been used for this work yet, and is shown as a possible extension for future investigation. It may be replaced altogether by <em>Gaia</em> colours, based on <em>G</em><sub>BP</sub> and <em>G</em><sub>RP</sub>, if these are available in future releases.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=94828293 id=\"94828293\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3-3>3.3 Foregrounds: Galactic substructure</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Where the stellar density is higher, e.g. at low Galactic latitudes, the <em>WISE</em>+<em>Gaia</em> multiplet search triggers more often. While this is a nuisance for quasar lens searches, it also means that it can be used to locate stellar overdensities such as satellite galaxies, globular clusters and streams. Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>, plotting multiplets among non-duplicate <em>Gaia</em> detections, shows some of these. Besides the Large Magellanic Cloud and the Orphan Stream, some Southern candidate streams appear. I designate them as WG1, with RA, Dec. \u2248(64.16, \u221223.2) to (97.2, \u221255.5); WG2, with RA, Dec. \u2248(70.5, \u221251.4) to (95.7, \u221247.1); WG3, with RA, Dec. \u2248(304.1, \u221247.7) to (351.3, \u221244.8) and WG4, with RA, Dec. \u2248(300.0, \u221249.4) to (333.5, \u221266.0). Of these, two (WG3, WG4) may have counterparts independently identified<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn5\" data-open=\"fn5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">5</a></sup><sup>\u2021</sup> in DES data (Shipp &amp; DES Collaboration, in preparation). The sharpest stream is WG1, WG2 is weaker and barely visible in the DES search,<sup>5</sup> and the thin stream WG3 seems to cross the Galactic plane, whereas WG4 is considerably thicker and may be a superposition of two, almost-parallel streams. Their quoted endpoints should be solely a guidance to the eye: they are not the primary aim of the <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> multiplet search and so they are roughly traced by the detected quasar+star alignments. Besides WG1, \u2026, WG4, the thin stream of Balbinot et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>) can be seen crossing the ATLAS and DES footprints.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Other candidate streams can be seen at low grazing angles from the Galactic plane, or in the ATLAS footprint, but are less sharp and may be given by patchy footprint coverage, as traced by the distribution of <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> quasar-like singlets. An example of spurious overdensity, in the Northern Galactic Hemisphere, is given by two wide regions with low <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> singlet density separated by a thin strip that has more complete coverage, which could otherwise be confused for a stream extending from RA, Dec. \u2248(160, 15)\u00a0deg to RA, Dec. \u2248(150, 45)\u00a0deg. The four candidates WG1, \u2026, WG4 seem more robust than others because they do not seemingly coincide with inhomogeneities in the <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> coverage: as shown by Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a> in the ratio of multiplets to singlets, the same overdensities corresponding to WG1, \u2026, WG4 remain once their distribution is normalized to that of singlets.</p>                        <a id=\"94828296\" scrollto-destination=\"94828296\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/471/2/10.1093_mnras_stx1650/1/m_stx1650fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611466529&amp;Signature=Vfa1WI3rSfGeqnuvilBeknyssrHTDSYmyv5yA~Gs6v2D85e~Oj5qgqU1q3FF2OGWkHNbyH0~BVxXi~CfTrhgiMh6UBYmMaSW3nm4j5wl0dXWK6tx8MwjtPiihFIFuglEP5xHF9W~47jzx3m~faMhYypT4HQzKdKSusC03d-P7BvexDtPHswhyKe8fOtJo9QMECqbvVIqw8NELZjPDYpABFukh86nLDYEigauBGHclvXm5k4e-0pa1e7NL-2H~M0FmbDF4sAAEL5iXn197DbaBdfx9~vRFKVpPoa5-1NdlNe1xQgnhyu2vA5suY7Z9pcLXh4wCHlQSdPjizGVnq3Hhg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Distribution of (non-duplicate) WISE\u2212Gaia singlets and multiplets over the pseudo-DES footprint. The edge of the MW disc is visible in the increased multiplet counts at low |b|.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig5.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/94828296/stx1650fig5.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig5.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"94828296\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/471/2/10.1093_mnras_stx1650/1/stx1650fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611466529&Signature=eFczXpGaTRAKStIJbL8xflWEXzFUXsc1KBMKneU8sUZrfdFQduC1zYR63nvEkP27PNl8e1IvHv4zNPgM3FqYuu9PnLgaq10-NqsTPJJAzdPmq1RY0uzQfOTXJM2WSXjDyxAtkvSrmivX43nDgIvf4H4Sraw732SLgTOPZdL0pFOqjAFStWw7t1GnQb0Xge88DjFPvlivE9k3i3kGxpckFHFdHxk4xGVecbVYz9II74N6fxlYoZqX-JkSyhwz-qH3FABSgJWPRm1vn6ettYcYhld3l3qY2SqxU66Af9~GwjP344hhEr52Tv9uagUtGcRyIrv3MCugulbL7Ar9vt6oGw__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=94828296&ar=3922852&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx1650fig5.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Distribution of (non-duplicate) <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> singlets and multiplets over the pseudo-DES footprint. <em>Top:</em> density of single matches; <em>bottom:</em> ratio of multiplets to singlets, showing the same inhomogeneities identified from Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>. The edge of the MW disc is visible in the increased multiplet counts at low |<em>b</em>|.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Given the primary scope of this paper, i.e. lensed quasar searches, the identification of WG1, \u2026, WG4 may be regarded as an unintended by-product. Searches for Galactic substructure via stellar overdensities have been applied extensively in the past to the SDSS (Belokurov et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Zucker et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib69\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib69\" data-open=\"bib69\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Belokurov et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>; Irwin et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>; Koposov et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib33\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib33\" data-open=\"bib33\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>; Belokurov et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>), ATLAS (Belokurov et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>) and DES (Bechtol et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Koposov et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib34\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib34\" data-open=\"bib34\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Balbinot et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>; Li et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib38\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib38\" data-open=\"bib38\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>) footprints, and have also led to the discovery of two star clusters using <em>Gaia</em> data alone (Koposov et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). Northern streams, dwarf galaxies and globular clusters have also been found as overdensities in the PS1 footprint (e.g. Laevens et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Bernard et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>, and references therein). The search outlined here differs from those as it targets neighbours within the same 6\u201310\u00a0arcsec radius, as opposed to overdensities on arc-minute scales from binned star counts.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Two steps forward may be envisioned, enabling an all-sky <em>WISE</em>+<em>Gaia</em> search of Galactic substructure down to the <em>G</em>\u00a0=\u00a020.7 detection limit. First, it may be tailored directly on stellar objects (<em>W</em>1\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>2 \u2272 0.3, instead of <em>W</em>1\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>2\u00a0&gt;\u00a00.55), and may also be augmented with 2MASS (Skrutskie et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib57\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib57\" data-open=\"bib57\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>) information, such as <em>J</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>1\u00a0&lt;\u00a01.2 (Vickers, R\u00f6ser &amp; Grebel\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib63\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib63\" data-open=\"bib63\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). The quasar-like colour selection and match to <em>Gaia</em> are, in fact, one reason for the circular gaps in the distribution of multiplets over the sky, due to crowding or higher extinction. Second, while WG1, \u2026, WG4 were identified solely based on visual inspection, a more complete search may automatically select associations of multiplets that lie on the same line over \u22485\u201310\u00a0deg-long distances. This would also help identify more diffuse streams from more massive projenitors, which (Balbinot &amp; Gieles\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) can otherwise be confused with random fluctuations in the distribution of halo stars.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Even fainter magnitudes may be reached by trading the resolution of <em>Gaia</em> with deeper <em>grizY</em> magnitudes from DES in the South or PS1 in the North. In this case, the <em>WISE</em> pre-selection might be dropped altogether, by-passing completeness limits at <em>i</em> \u2273 21; however, a quasar-like <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia singlet</em> selection is still useful to characterize the survey coverage, and hence evaluate spurious substructure detections.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=94828300 id=\"94828300\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 CONCLUSIONS AND FUTURE PROSPECTS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">I have introduced two new methods to find quasar lenses, and illustrated their performance on publicly accessible footprints, using training- and test sets of known lenses and pairs in the CASTLES and SQLS data bases. The first concentrates on objects that are not well described as isolated quasars or blue galaxies; the second joins <em>WISE</em> and <em>Gaia</em> to detect multiplets of point-sources with overall quasar mid-IR colours. Besides recovering known lenses (with varying degree of success), both searches have led to new discoveries, reported elsewhere. A by-product of the <em>WISE</em>+<em>Gaia</em> search has been the identification of Galactic stream candidates that (as I later learned) are being found within the DES collaboration using different techniques.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">A common feature of many searches, including the outlier-selection and multiplet-detection, is the trade-off between completeness and manageable size of candidate samples to be visually inspected and followed-up at the telescope. Searches concentrating on \u2018lens\u2019 colours (e.g. this outlier-selection and the population-mixture classification by Williams et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib65\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib65\" data-open=\"bib65\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017a</a>) discard a high fraction of lenses with colours akin to nearby unlensed quasars. This is a price to pay in order to find systems with sources at higher redshift, or that could not be pre-selected for SDSS fibre spectroscopy due to their unusual colours. On the other hand, searches tailored on \u2018quasar\u2019 colours, amending the loss of lenses with quasar-like colours, result in large candidate samples to be examined: according to Ostrovski et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib47\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib47\" data-open=\"bib47\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), a double was found after eyeballing 5000 objects brighter than <em>i</em>\u00a0=\u00a019 in a 1500\u00a0deg<sup>2</sup> footprint. By comparison, the outlier selection resulted in 5064 SDSS targets brighter than <em>i</em>\u00a0=\u00a020.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The pseudo-distance cuts reduce the number of objects considerably, from 5\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>5</sup> to \u22488600 targets, of which \u224860\u2009per\u2009cent non-repeated objects, down to 239 final candidates, to the price of a harsh selection on known lenses. Even though few systems are rejected by each pair-wise combination of pseudo-distances, and most of the rejected lenses lie close to the cut boundaries, all cuts combined reduce the overall completeness to 30\u2009per\u2009cent, or 50\u2009per\u2009cent when only cuts in <em>d</em><sub>1</sub>, \u2026, <em>d</em><sub>4</sub> are used. Since the number of targets for visual inspection is manageable, one could loosen the cuts in <em>d</em><sub>5</sub>, \u2026, <em>d</em><sub>10</sub>; this would mean that the whole test set would now be a training-set for the method. Despite the 50\u2009per\u2009cent completeness with respect to already-known lenses, previously unknown lenses have been discovered with this technique (e.g. the new quad J1433+60; Agnello et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017b</a>), which suggests that outlier-selection is indeed complementary to previous searches.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Comparable numbers, from query to final candidates, are found when applying the <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> search to the SDSS footprint. The resolving power of <em>Gaia</em> enables multiplet detection for objects that are otherwise blended by the pipelines of ground-based surveys. New lenses, not found by other techniques, have been discovered with this method and will be presented elsewhere. Its performance, however, is not obvious to characterize: while it recognizes the two quasar images of the close double DES J0115 (Agnello et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015b</a>), and all quasar images of the fold PG1115 (Weymann et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib64\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib64\" data-open=\"bib64\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1980</a>), it detects only two images in the DES J0408 quad (Lin et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib39\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib39\" data-open=\"bib39\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), and two the WFI2033 quad (Morgan et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>), whereas the WFI2026 quad is seemingly unresolved. Due to <em>G</em>\u00a0=\u00a020.7 depth and pipeline-specific choices in resolving close pairs with high flux-ratios, roughly one every three known lenses/pairs is resolved by <em>Gaia</em>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Hybrid colours may be used as additional information, either using (limited) ground-based information or via <em>G</em><sub>RP</sub>, <em>G</em><sub>BP</sub> photometry, if available in future releases. This will be particularly interesting in view of the EUCLID mission, which should provide a wide-field, deep and sharp counterpart to the slitless spectroscopic Hamburg-ESO survey (Wisotzki et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib66\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib66\" data-open=\"bib66\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>), from which some remarkable quasar lenses have been identified.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Classification via clustering and outlier-selection has been implemented with different methods, for other purposes, over the last 2\u00a0yr. Clustering in colour-space has been used to evaluate photometric redshifts (Rahman et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib49\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib49\" data-open=\"bib49\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016b</a>; Rahman, M\u00e9nard &amp; Scranton\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib48\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib48\" data-open=\"bib48\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016a</a>), select LRGs (Rozo et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib51\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib51\" data-open=\"bib51\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>) and identify galaxy clusters from improved red-sequence finders (Rykoff et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib52\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib52\" data-open=\"bib52\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). Outlier-selection, implemented via random-forest classification on SDSS fibre spectra of galaxies, has been used to select peculiar galaxies of various types (Baron &amp; Poznanski\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). While the search in this paper was tailored on (lensed) quasars, and others were concentrated on galaxies, there is significant scope for integrating these into a comprehensive photometric classification across wide-field surveys and selection of the most peculiar objects.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">A by-product of the <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> multiplet search is the detection of (candidate) Milky Way streams, as coherent structures traced by stars in front of <em>WISE</em> quasar candidates. Multi-band follow-up is needed, however, to confirm them and characterize their stellar populations. A <em>WISE</em>\u2212<em>Gaia</em> search can be tailored on streams, using a different <em>WISE</em> selection and possibly augmenting with near-IR colours to separate extragalactic objects.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=94828308 id=\"94828308\" class=\"backacknowledgements-title\" >Acknowledgments</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">I wish to thank Eduardo Balbinot, Nora Shipp, Alex Drlica-Wagner for the comparison between my MW stream candidates and theirs; and Elizabeth Buckley-Geer, Huan Lin, Paul Schechter and Tommaso Treu for discussions on quasar lens searches. cause table not important": ""}}}}}}, "Paper Overview": {"authors": ["Agnello, Adriano"], "journal_name": "Monthly Notices of the Royal Astronomical Society", "type_of_reference": "JOUR", "abstract": "I describe two novel techniques originally devised to select strongly lensed quasar candidates in wide-field surveys. The first relies on outlier selection in optical and mid-infrared magnitude space; the second combines mid-infrared colour selection with Gaia spatial resolution, to identify multiplets of objects with quasar-like colours. Both methods have already been applied successfully to the Sloan Digital Sky Survey, ATLAS and Dark Energy Survey footprints: besides recovering known lenses from previous searches, they have led to new discoveries, including quadruply lensed quasars, which are rare within the rare-object class of quasar lenses. As a serendipitous by-product, at least four candidate Galactic streams in the South have been identified among foreground contaminants. There is considerable scope for tailoring the WISE-Gaia multiplet search to stellar-like objects, instead of quasar-like, and to automatically detect Galactic streams.", "doi": "10.1093/mnras/stx1650", "start_page": "2013", "number": "2", "publication_year": "2017/10/1", "end_page": "2021", "custom1": "eprint: arXiv:1705.08900", "author_address": ["AA(European Southern Observatory, Karl-Schwarzschild-Strasse 2, D-85748 Garching bei M\u00fcnchen, Germany)"], "keywords": ["gravitational lensing: strong", "methods: statistical", "surveys", "Galaxy: structure", "Astrophysics - Astrophysics of Galaxies", "Astrophysics - Cosmology and Nongalactic Astrophysics"], "url": "https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2017MNRAS.471.2013A", "volume": "471", "Title": "Quasar lenses and galactic streams: outlier selection and Gaia multiplet detection", "issn": "0035-8711"}}
